<Review>Went here given good reviews. Neither my girlfriend nor I liked it. The sushi was 80%+ rice - the Caterpillar roll barely had any eel, one of the 8 pieces literally had none (just rice, a carrot and a cucumber slice). They also use a poor tasting (in our opinion) imitation crab, lots of it, in all there rolls. No brown rice option. And tons of mayo in their rolls, even when not listed as an ingredient on the menu.

The servers are friendly but speak little English. The atmosphere is very basic.

Definitely prefer PB Sushi, Zen 5, or any of the other sushi places on Garnet.< /Review><pics>None< /pics>< resp>

One of the worst restaurant experiences

I went here on a Wednesday night, the place was packed. This isn't hard to do though seeing the restaurant is maybe 300 sq feet and you're eating on top of your neighbor.

However the night got worse when a drunk birthday girl who couldn't stand came in with her two friends and sat down next to us. The entire time she was there she kept screaming at the top of her lungs it was her birthday, for a solid hour. The staff did not kick her out or tell her to be quiet because she was disrupting everyone... instead they continued to serve her.

Meanwhile I see the sushi chefs pissed with her and whispering and laughing while they made their tables rolls. The one saying no no don't and the other laughing and messing with the food.

I would never come here again due to the service, the atmosphere and lack of trust to the chefs who are in view of the public.<//text>

<Time>1574362591630</Time>< rating>
5< /rating>
< review>
It's a great place to hike to from Eaton Canyon... If you're NEW pay attention! There is a "contributor" Tatiana Lopez that appears to have uploaded 2500+ photos and tagged them as being taken at Henninger Flats. They are NOT properly tagged... and I've exhausted reported as many as I can... but it will take forever! So just ignore her photos... there is a very obvious difference in her photos verses what others have posted/tagged.

For those Hiking up from Eaton Canyon... it is a challenging elevation climb, but an easy hike as the trail is quite clear and wide. The trail is the "fire road" that leads up to Henninger (which was repaired a number of years ago after a landslide took out large portions of the road (and mountain side)... I'm glad it was reopened... and for those wanting a big challenge you can continue up to Mt. Wilson if you're feeling bold!

Remember to "leave no trace" and keep your 10 essentials with you. This is still wild country with spiders, snakes, bears and mountain lions in the area. So please, don't treat your hike as if you're going to Tom Sawyer Island and Disneyland. You can get hurt if you're not being safe. People have fallen from ledges and been hurt (a few killed) so treat nature with respect and stay firmly on the trails.

YIS,
-Bradley</review>

<Review>In May I made the move from Seattle to Los Angeles and it didn’t take long for me to start itching to get outdoors and explore. Unfortunately it took me a couple weeks to settle in and finally make time to get out. I started doing some research on recommended places to camp near LA and Henniger Flats was at the top of almost everyone’s list that I could find online. A short hike, free camping and not far from where I live; sold. Especially for my first camping adventure since making the move to sunny California.

Henniger Flats is located in the San Gabriel Mountains near Altadena, California. Directions on getting there are pretty simple coming from downtown LA.

The trailhead to Henniger Flats is located off N Altadena Drive. It’s not easy to spot but if you’re familiar with the area, you’ll probably have no problem finding it. If you’re heading to Henniger Flats for the night, you’ll have to pay attention to where you park because there’s not a lot of overnight or long-term parking at the trailhead. I personally parked down the street on N Altadena in the neighborhood. Just keep an eye out for parking signs and you’ll probably be ok.

When you reach the trailhead you’ll see a sign that reads, “The Henniger Flats Project.” You have to hike up  Mount Wilson Toll Road to get there. Initially it’s a little confusing to figure out which trail you need to be on to get there, at least it was for me. You’ll walk down the beginning of the trail and cross the white bridge. Once you cross the white bridge, stay to the left and head up until you reach Henniger Flats. It’s about a 3 mile hike and the incline gets steep at times. There are plenty of benches to rest at on the way up.

There’s no shade on the way up so it’s important to start your hike early if you intend on camping and have a heavy pack. Also bring an abundance of water. There is a visitor center and museum at Henniger Flats, but there’s no running water. Be prepared! I didn’t run into any wildlife and you probably won’t either since the trail is very popular and there seems to be a lot of foot traffic throughout the day. There are a few signs for rattlesnakes but I didn’t run into any.

After your 3 mile journey to the top, you’ve reached Henniger Flats. First thing’s first, you need to find the onsite LACFD Forester that’s on duty to check in. I read that you’ll be given a permit for camping and to use a stove, but I didn’t have to do that when I checked in for whatever reason. There was a cub scout clan doing some work at the campgrounds so I’m sure he was busy and distracted. After or even before you check in, you can check out the visitor center and museum to learn about Henniger Flats and the surrounding areas. It’s pretty neat.

Once you get checked in you’ll have to find your camping lot. There are 3 levels of camping at Henniger Flats. There’s a lower level campground near the visitor center and museum. It seemed pretty busy, so I walked to the upper and Fiji campgrounds. The forester actually recommended the Fiji campground area for a quieter environment and great place for setting up hammocks. He was absolutely right and if you’re looking for a quiet place to chillax, Fiji is the way to go.

Most larger camping lots have picnic tables and stoves to cook on. It’s worth noting there are about 15-20 camping lots in the upper and lower campgrounds. Fiji only has 3 camping lots, so you have to get there early to snag one. You can also call the forester head of time to get some insight on open camp lots. There’s plenty of shade once you get settled and the campgrounds are very well kept. There was no trash, the trails were well maintained and the views are phenomenal. There’s plenty of trails to check out after you get settled in.

Overall I had a great experience camping at Henniger Flats and I will certainly go again. #LosAngeles #Hiking #Outdoors<//Review>< gmapID>

<Review>I love these guys. I have a BMW Z4 and used to go to Santa Palm (until they left circular scuffs on my hood and a friends hood in separate instances) and then moved to the carwash on Sunset (until they closed because of covid). I've been searching for someone solid that I trust with my car and was told to try ECO Mobile. Very glad I did.
These guys are great. My Car always comes back looking dope. I had CRAZY hard water spots from a sprinkler once and I could not get them out anywhere. Reese promised he could get them out with a detail and, though I was skeptical, his guys delivered in a big way. The car looked brand new. They are now my trusted go-to when washing my car - I won't go anywhere else.
It is important to note that they are in the parking garage of a sometimes busy shopping plaza. It may take a little longer when bringing your car here but, in my mind, that just means they are being detailed with the car. There's a ton to do upstairs while you wait (go see a movie, grocery shop, have lunch, buy furniture, get a haircut...). They call you when your car is ready and validate. Can't go wrong here.</Review>< pictures>

Called ahead to make sure they had time for us. They asked all the right questions and told us to come in. They let us know there was a $65 diagnostic fee that is essentially a deposit. Basically, if you have them do the work, they apply it to the bill. If you have them do the diagnostic work but decide to walk, you gotta pay $65. Pretty reasonable.

The car was stalling periodically so they ran it. They ran it on blocks with some gas. They took it out and drove it. They checked the fluids and topped them up. They cleaned the carbon buildup on all the parts of the fuel and exhaust system that could be contributing to the stalls. If nothing else, it's idling much smoother. When we picked up the car, they popped the hood, talked us through what they saw and where, and let us ask questions.

What did all this cost us? Just the $65 diagnostic fee. I'm super happy. Great value, they were receptive to questions and talking is through what they saw. I'll be going back for sure.< /text>

< Review>
My first experience with Al's Auto Center was fantastic!! I don't know much about cars, even my own, so going to a mechanic tends to make me anxious, but Augustin was awesome and helped walk me through the whole experience.

My 8 year old Honda Fit started making weird metal on metal noises a few weeks ago. This is my first car and since I couldn't identify the noise, I took it to a Honda dealership and asked them to look to make sure nothing was wrong. The service provider at the dealership called to tell me that my transmission was the issue and that it would be $4,400 to replace it!!! I only came in because there was a strange noise, my car was driving perfectly fine.

Everyone suggested getting a second opinion, and after a quick google and reading a few reviews I called Al's Auto Center and asked about bringing my car in for them to check my transmission. I actually called Al's 3 times before I had the time to come in, and each time they answered the phone quickly and answered all of my questions. I called today and they said to bring my car around in an hour, so that is what I did.

When I arrived at Al's Auto Center, I met Augustin. I explained what the dealership told me and told him about the noise. He asked if he could drive around the block with me to hear the noise. I drove him down a few streets and he said he heard the noise. However, he said he didn't think it was the transmission because the car was shifting without a problem. After explaining everything to me, he said he would lift up my car and take a look underneath.

Once under my car, he showed me how my catalytic converter was what was rattling when my car idled, and showed me where my transmission was. I had never seen the underside of my car like that, and Augustin talked me through what I was looking at while explaining what he believed was making the noise. When he brought the car down, Augustin checked my transmission fluid and took the time to show me what the difference between new and used fluid looked like. Because of everything he showed me and the lack of information from the dealership, I feel pretty confident in Augustin's opinion.

And in the end, Augustin recommended that I not worry about the noise until the car started to actually drive differently and to bring it by any time I was worried and they would check it again. I will certainly be happy to bring my car back here if it has any problems!</Review>

The longer version is... I moved to LA last year and didn't have anyone to take care of my cat when I travel (which is frequent.) I found FETCH online and figured I'd give them a try based on all the positive reviews. Now, 10 months later, I'm recommending them to my friends and neighbors. <Review>My wife and I hired FETCH PET CARE of Los Angeles Westside to arrange for a petsitter to stay in our home and watch over our beloved animal companions while we're out of town. We were impressed by their reviews on Google and Yelp. Their website claims "Fetch Pet Care's experienced sitters are background checked, bonded, and insured pet lovers." They quickly set us up with their sitter/walker named Anthony (Tony) Vercillo who outwardly seemed like a good candidate to take good care of our dog & cat. So, we agreed to book him for the 10 days we'd be away.

In the late morning of day 7, our cleaning crew came in for a routine sprucing and they were so shocked by the ill state of the apartment they felt compelled to contact us. They texted me photos of feces and urine left in various rooms, beer cans & liquor bottles filled our recycling bin, piles of garbage spilling onto the floor and other examples of disarray uncharacteristic to us and our pets. They also told us that a woman was in the apartment with the sitter (although that had not been permitted by us), and another dog that didn't belong to us.

Alarmed by the situation but thinking it can still be handled rather easily, I called Fetch Pet Care to have them address the situation.  They told me they would replace the current pet sitter with a more responsible person as quickly and uneventfully as possible. What I didn't know was that the representative from Fetch Pet Care would soon make an irreversible management error that would threaten the security of our dog, cat and home.

The Fetch representative called the sitter first to confront him about the situation over the phone, while he still had our dog with him. We found out later that this confrontation then led the sitter to openly put the blame on the woman who was with him and that the woman quickly became unhinged as a result. They argued and then she suddenly disappeared with our sweet, sensitive dog.

We were scared out of our minds, though, not knowing what was going on with our poor dog but we couldn't do much else but wait. At some point, we were eventually told that the kidnapper was a diagnosed schizophrenic and possibly more unstable than we'd initially imagined. We were worried sick about any possible misstep that could cause a big reaction from this woman. We kept calling the police, the park rangers, the Fetch representative and even the sitter for updates but for many hours none came. A couple hours later, the woman contacted the sitter again and this time she demanded ransom money from him in exchange for our dog's safe return.

Late in the evening, our dog was finally turned over to a representative of Fetch Pet Care.  We cut our trip short and returned the very next day.  Upon our return we took our dog to the vet for a checkup and though her general heath was okay, she had lost 4lbs in during those 7 days and was slightly anemic.  Our cat also looked as if he hadn't been fed in several days but other than that he was fine. Our home was mostly restored by a thorough cleaning. So we're okay. But we're not okay. This never should happen to anyone.

Fetch refunded our money and paid for the additional expenses we incurred as a result of this ordeal. While we are trying to be accepting of this gesture, it doesn't come close to repaying us for this horror of a day that never would have happened if only they had managed their human resources issue in a more sensible, secure way. Nor would any of this happened if they had properly vetted this sitter before touting him to all of their clients as an appropriate caregiver. I seriously question every decent review for this company and warn everyone to stay far away from the caregiver named Anthony (Tony) Vercillo. He will trash your home, fail to feed your pets, fail to walk your dog regularly, fail to clean the litter box, and expose your furry loved ones to a dognapper.</Review>< resp>

<date>1567741454607< /date>< rating>
3</rating>
<text>This is a gluten free review.

Gluten free menu: No, but GF items clearly marked

Gluten free options: 5/5
Pretty much the entire menu is gluten free. I really appreciate that they itemize all major allergens for every item on their menu.

I do plan on asking if their falafels are actually gluten free but maybe just fried in a shared fryer. If they are gluten free then I look forward to trying them the next time around.

Food: 2/5
Portions are good for one person. Everything tasted fresh and very healthy, but kind of bland. Also, I'm a white meat chicken eater and just wasn't a fan of the meat quality. I had quite a bit of dark meat and some cartilage in my bowl, which was pretty unappetizing.

Service: 4/5
Staff was friendly and helpful at explaining how to order and what they would recommend combining in the bowl (especially sauces...there's so many options).

Location: 4/5
Super easy to park and find the restaurant

Ambiance: 3/5
Comfortable. Nothing special. Feels like any other fast food restaurant setting.

Price: 3/5
About $15 per person with a drink

Overall score: 3/5

I'll come back and give Cava one more try. Hope its a better experience the second time around.< /text><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOs0m41t6rz-vA17Ym0PGZc89U4ZnuG7cndrQYs=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPtCRMNivZ3GQqEpTtgLwWzYwNEPlJS86lb9PTj=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOdtfByqGdEV9tRIY2xxjZz61GQANvvzmqDtbkw=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNEisKgLZSaW_8Xr4mKB238hTB-cS2HrV0GvRP4=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPte4otlEDuWPL0LWML59wyMNYMVqigsEUnFXoE=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPoHgT_AqRKTtZCOpRZfhqJhNXBYKV8Jqt-c46z=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNHRdTpRht24HeXBPrXaiXVvFleDA7p8GiwTRxp=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOxbebkZktdACsYtQMqp_qBOznJ5IAZUh0OWKG5=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPqKYqfkg3WexYBPK9OeU0J_6ipuiBy42Z1pBZb=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pics>< response>

<Review>This is a gluten free review.

Gluten free menu: No, but GF items clearly marked

Gluten free options: 5/5
Pretty much the entire menu is gluten free. I really appreciate that they itemize all major allergens for every item on their menu.

I do plan on asking if their falafels are actually gluten free but maybe just fried in a shared fryer. If they are gluten free then I look forward to trying them the next time around.

Food: 2/5
Portions are good for one person. Everything tasted fresh and very healthy, but kind of bland. Also, I'm a white meat chicken eater and just wasn't a fan of the meat quality. I had quite a bit of dark meat and some cartilage in my bowl, which was pretty unappetizing.

Service: 4/5
Staff was friendly and helpful at explaining how to order and what they would recommend combining in the bowl (especially sauces...there's so many options).

Location: 4/5
Super easy to park and find the restaurant

Ambiance: 3/5
Comfortable. Nothing special. Feels like any other fast food restaurant setting.

Price: 3/5
About $15 per person with a drink

Overall score: 3/5

I'll come back and give Cava one more try. < Review>
This is one of our favorite spot for a quick healthy meal. It’s the same concept as Chipotle, but we feel like we get way more food from Cava than we do at chipotle. I can never finish my bowl and end up having two meals out of it. You get 4 different options for greens and 3 options for grains. You also get pita bread without any extra charge. My favorite part of building this bowl are the dips. I always get one scoop of the crazy feta and two scoops of the harissa. For the meats we always pick the chicken and braised lamb. After the proteins, you get to add unlimited toppings such as, Pickled onions, banana peppers, olives, cucumber tomato salad, tabbouleh and a few other items. Lastly, it’s the sauce! We always cover our bowls and ask for extra of the green harissa sauce. The service is always very quick. They get you in and out! Sometimes the greens can be a little dry because it’s been sitting out for too long. So be sure to ask for a fresh batch! And depending on the server, sometimes they don’t give you enough grains or greens so be sure to ask for more of that too!<//Review>

Love this place! Fresh food, great taste, really good options that are both healthy and delicious. Their kids meal is also a good value and allows for lots of choices.

< Review>
The food taste good but the portions are a bit off. They hardly provide any meat, we're talking 2 small meatballs if you order half meatballs. And when you order a grains and greens bowl, they put like a half a spoon of rice, its like a bad joke. The bill ends up being like $14 just for a bowl of food, and if you don't top it with all of the extras, you'll be very disappointed in how little meat and rice actually comes with the bowl. Since you are forced to top the bowl with some extras so that you can actually feel satisfied with your meal, by the time you eat, all the meat is cold as the temperatures have mixed.

All around, I will not be coming back to CAVA due to the expensive price for a not-so-satisfying meal.</Review>

<Gmap_id>0x80dcdc34352478d7:0x20017cf4f2a12ff8< /Gmap_id><user_name>Charlton Bilow</user_name><UserId.>113730223317010638474< /UserId.><date>1485873792208</date><Rating>5</Rating>< Pics>
None<//Pics>
<Review>I love this place! A Paleo friendly, quick Chipotle style service, low prices and convenient. It can't be topped. I had this in Washington DC and wished it was in California and now we have it! I love it. There are many great savory and spicy options which keep it fresh and new every visit.

Your base: has 8 options, lentils, white rice, brown rice, arugula, romaine, baby spinach,  super greens mix, mesclun mix. There's no place that has as many quality leafy green options to choose from. They allow you to mix and match. My favorite is the super greens with kale brussel sprouts, broccoli, chicory, and cabbage.

The dips: They give you 3 sides to choose from out of 6 options: Hummus , a roasted red pepper hummus , tzaziki, eggplant and red pepper, crazy feta, harrisa. In my opinion, all the options taste good. When I say they taste good, I don't mean ok. Compared to other foods of this kind, they excel.

Meat: Choose 1 from 6 options. They do have a veggie option for vegetarians. I tried the lamb meat balls and chicken. Both tasted great. The meat balls were a little dry, but that's not uncommon with this style. They offer: veggies, chicken, lamb meatballs, beef, shredded lamb (very juicy) , and beef meatballs.

Dressing/Topping: I believe they have six options. I don't remember the names of any of them. I tried two and both were great tasting.

Bonus: They have pleasant service here. Washington DC isn't known for its service where this chain has many of its locations.</Review></record></dataset><record>

<Review>I was looking for a healthy option for lunch, and found the newly opened Cava Grill.
This is a build-your-own kind of eatery with Meditarrean food.
It was my first time there, and the staff was very friendly and helpful.
The restaurant was open and bright.

There are 5 steps to order. Everything is listed on the menu.
First you can pick if you want greens, grain, pita, or a combination of things.
Second you pick the dips and spreads.
Third is picking the proteins.
Then the toppings.
Lastly the dressings.

Here were my choices:
(1) Greens + Grains - SuperGreens, Brown Basmati Rice;
(2) Tzatziki, Roasted Red Pepper Hummus, Crazy Feta;
(3) Chicken + Grilled Meatballs;
(4) Tomato, Cucumber, Cabbage Slaw, Pickled Onions, Pickled Banana Peppers, Kalamata Olives, Crumbled Feta, Fresh Mint
(5) Lemon Herb Tahini, Green Harissa.

This bowl of goodies was so delicious!
It was like flavor explosion in my mouth.
Everything was good. All the meat, sauces, dips, veggies, salad, grains.. everything!
I chowed down the whole bowl, was completely full, but I wanted even more.

I am so in love with this restaurant.
Can't wait to go back again!!<//Review><pictures>None</pictures>< resp>
